<p>The <b>United States Border Patrol</b> (<b>USBP</b>) is the United States <a href="/wiki/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection" title="U.S. Customs and Border Protection">Customs and Border Protection</a>'s federal law enforcement arm within the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">United States Department of Homeland Security</a> (DHS). The USBP is the armed and uniformed federal police that secure the borders of the United States by detecting and preventing <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration" title="Illegal immigration">illegal aliens</a>, terrorists and terrorist weapons from entering the United States, and prevent illegal trafficking of people and contraband.<sup id="cite_ref-CPB_overview_20080822_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPB_overview_20080822-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CBP_20150918_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBP_20150918-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With 19,437 agents,<sup id="cite_ref-politifact.com_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politifact.com-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> the Border Patrol is one of the largest law enforcement agencies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> For fiscal year 2017, Congress enacted a budget of $3,805,253,000 for the Border Patrol.<sup id="cite_ref-FY2017sectors_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY2017sectors-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The current chief of the Border Patrol is <a href="/wiki/Carla_Provost" title="Carla Provost">Carla Provost</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USnews_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USnews-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Mounted watchmen of the United States Department of Commerce and Labor patrolled the border in an effort to prevent illegal crossings as early as 1904, but their efforts were irregular and undertaken only when resources permitted. The inspectors, usually called "mounted guards", operated out of El Paso, Texas. Though they never totaled more than 75, they patrolled as far west as California trying to restrict the flow of illegal Chinese immigration.
</p><p>In March 1915, Congress authorized a separate group of mounted guards, often referred to as "mounted inspectors". Most rode on horseback, but a few operated automobiles, motorcycles and boats. Although these inspectors had broader arrest authority, they still largely pursued Chinese aliens trying to avoid the National Origins Act and Chinese Exclusion Act of 1882. These patrolmen were Immigration Inspectors, assigned to inspection stations, and could not watch the border at all times. U.S. Army soldiers along the southwest border performed intermittent border patrolling, but this was secondary to "the more serious work of military training." Aliens encountered illegally in the U.S. by the Army were directed to the immigration inspection stations. Texas Rangers were also sporadically assigned to patrol duties by the state, and their efforts were noted as "singularly effective".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">The current badge after the agency became a part Homeland Security (2003–)</div></div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BorderPatrol.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/BorderPatrol.png/220px-BorderPatrol.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/BorderPatrol.png/330px-BorderPatrol.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/BorderPatrol.png/440px-BorderPatrol.png 2x" data-file-width="1320" data-file-height="968" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BorderPatrol.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>During the 1940 Border Patrol expansion, four newly hired agents from the northeastern states drove this new pursuit vehicle from the Ford factory in Detroit to El Paso where they would receive training.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2ndThompsonTraining.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/2ndThompsonTraining.png/220px-2ndThompsonTraining.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/2ndThompsonTraining.png/330px-2ndThompsonTraining.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/2ndThompsonTraining.png/440px-2ndThompsonTraining.png 2x" data-file-width="1248" data-file-height="1134" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2ndThompsonTraining.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Border Patrol Agent practice firing a Thompson submachine gun near El Paso in 1940.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Origins_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="National Origins Act">National Origins Act</a> authorized the formation of the U.S. Border Patrol on May 26, 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnic_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnic-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Two days later, the <b>Labor Appropriation Act of 1924</b> established the Border Patrol as an agency of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Labor" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Department of Labor">U.S. Department of Labor</a> assigned to prevent <a href="/wiki/Illegal_entry" title="Illegal entry">illegal entries</a><sup id="cite_ref-CBP-4-2014_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBP-4-2014-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>—primarily along the <a href="/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Mexico–United States border">Mexico–United States border</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ethnic_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnic-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Canada–United States border">Canada–U.S. border</a>. The first Border Patrol station began operations in Detroit, Michigan in June 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> A second station in El Paso, Texas, began operations in July 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In 1925, coastal patrols began as well.<sup id="cite_ref-CBP-4-2014_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBP-4-2014-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Operations were established along the Gulf Coast in 1927 to ensure that foreign crewmen departed on the same ship on which they arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In 1932, the Border Patrol was divided into two offices. Mexican border operations were directed from <a href="/wiki/El_Paso,_Texas" title="El Paso, Texas">El Paso, Texas</a>, and Canadian border operations were directed from <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>. The Canadian border operations from Detroit employed more men than the El Paso operations along the Mexican border because of a focus on the prevention of liquor smuggling during prohibition. <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Delano_Roosevelt" class="mw-redirect" title="Franklin Delano Roosevelt">Franklin Delano Roosevelt</a>'s Executive Order 6166 formed the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Naturalization_Service" title="Immigration and Naturalization Service">Immigration and Naturalization Service</a> (INS) in 1933 by consolidation of the Bureau of Immigration and the Bureau of Naturalization. Following the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> in Europe, Border Patrol staffing doubled to 1,500 in 1940, and the INS was moved from the Department of Labor to the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Department of Justice">U.S. Department of Justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Additional stations were temporarily added along the Gulf Coast, Florida and the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">Eastern Seaboard</a> during the 1960s after Fidel Castro triumphed in the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> and that was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a>. INS was decommissioned in March 2003 when its operations were divided between CBP, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Citizenship_and_Immigration_Services" title="United States Citizenship and Immigration Services">United States Citizenship and Immigration Services</a>, and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Immigration_and_Customs_Enforcement" title="U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement">U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement</a>.
</p><p>In the wake of the attacks of September 11, the Border Patrol was placed under the umbrella of the Department of Homeland Security, and preventing terrorists and terrorist weapons from entering the United States was added to its mission. The Border Patrol's traditional mission continued: deterring, detecting and apprehending illegal aliens and individuals involved in the illegal drug trade who generally entered the United States at places other than through designated <a href="/wiki/Ports_of_entry" class="mw-redirect" title="Ports of entry">ports of entry</a>. The Border Patrol also erected<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2014)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> 33 permanent <a href="/wiki/United_States_Border_Patrol_Interior_Checkpoints" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Border Patrol Interior Checkpoints">interior checkpoints</a> near the southern border of the United States.
</p><p>For fiscal year 2017, the nationwide total of Border Patrol agents was 19,437, with 16,605 patrolling the southern border.<sup id="cite_ref-politifact.com_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politifact.com-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Agents primarily patrol the <a href="/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Mexico–United States border">Mexico–United States border</a>, where they control drug trafficking and illegal immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-who_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The majority of Border Patrol agents are <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">minorities</a>. According to 2016 data, <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Latinos</a> constitute slightly more than 50% of the Border Patrol.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Strategy">Strategy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Strategy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1986:_Employer_sanctions_and_interior_enforcement">1986: Employer sanctions and interior enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1986: Employer sanctions and interior enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:United_States_Border_Patrol_Mexico.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/United_States_Border_Patrol_Mexico.jpg/220px-United_States_Border_Patrol_Mexico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/United_States_Border_Patrol_Mexico.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="150" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_States_Border_Patrol_Mexico.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Border Patrol Agents with a <a href="/wiki/Hummer" title="Hummer">Hummer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter_AS350_%C3%89cureuil" title="Eurocopter AS350 Écureuil">Astar</a> patrol for illegal entry into the United States</div></div></div>
<p>The Border Patrol's priorities have changed over the years. In 1986, the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_Reform_and_Control_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigration Reform and Control Act">Immigration Reform and Control Act</a> placed renewed emphasis on controlling illegal immigration by going after the employers that hire illegal aliens. The belief was that jobs were the magnet that attracted most illegal aliens to come to the United States. The Border Patrol increased interior enforcement and Form I-9 audits of businesses through an inspection program known as "employer sanctions". Several agents were assigned to interior stations, such as within the <a href="/wiki/Livermore_Sector_(U.S._Border_Patrol)" title="Livermore Sector (U.S. Border Patrol)">Livermore Sector</a> in Northern California.
</p><p>Employer sanctions never became the effective tool it was expected to be by Congress. Illegal immigration continued to swell after the 1986 amnesty despite employer sanctions. By 1993, Californians passed <a href="/wiki/Proposition_187" class="mw-redirect" title="Proposition 187">Proposition 187</a>, denying benefits to illegal aliens and criminalizing illegal aliens in possession of forged green cards, identification cards, and Social Security numbers. It also authorized police officers to question non-nationals as to their immigration status and required police and sheriff departments to cooperate and report illegal aliens to the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Naturalization_Service" title="Immigration and Naturalization Service">INS</a>. Proposition 187 drew nationwide attention to illegal immigration.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Checkpoint_stations">Checkpoint stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Checkpoint stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/United_States_Border_Patrol_Interior_Checkpoints" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Border Patrol Interior Checkpoints">United States Border Patrol Interior Checkpoints</a> are inspection stations operated by the USBP within 100 miles (160&#160;km) of an international border (with Mexico or Canada) or any U.S. coastline, or in the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="El_Paso_Sector.27s_Operation_Hold_the_Line"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="El_Paso_Sector's_Operation_Hold_the_Line">El Paso Sector's Operation Hold the Line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: El Paso Sector&#039;s Operation Hold the Line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/El_Paso,_Texas" title="El Paso, Texas">El Paso</a> Sector Chief Patrol Agent <a href="/wiki/Silvestre_Reyes" title="Silvestre Reyes">Silvestre Reyes</a> started a program called "Operation Hold the Line". In this program, Border Patrol agents would no longer react to <a href="/wiki/Illegal_entry" title="Illegal entry">illegal entries</a> resulting in apprehensions, but would instead be forward deployed to the border, immediately detecting any attempted entries or deterring crossing at a more remote location. The idea was that it would be easier to capture illegal entrants in the wide open deserts than through the urban alleyways. Chief Reyes deployed his agents along the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a>, within eyesight of other agents. The program significantly reduced illegal entries in the urban part of El Paso, however, the operation merely shifted the illegal entries to other areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="San_Diego_Sector.27s_Operation_Gatekeeper"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="San_Diego_Sector's_Operation_Gatekeeper">San Diego Sector's Operation Gatekeeper</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: San Diego Sector&#039;s Operation Gatekeeper">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Border_patrol_at_the_beach,_San_Diego_county.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Border_patrol_at_the_beach%2C_San_Diego_county.jpg/220px-Border_patrol_at_the_beach%2C_San_Diego_county.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Border_patrol_at_the_beach%2C_San_Diego_county.jpg/330px-Border_patrol_at_the_beach%2C_San_Diego_county.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Border_patrol_at_the_beach%2C_San_Diego_county.jpg/440px-Border_patrol_at_the_beach%2C_San_Diego_county.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Border_patrol_at_the_beach,_San_Diego_county.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Patrolling the beach in San Diego County, California</div></div></div>
<p>Congressman <a href="/wiki/Duncan_L._Hunter" title="Duncan L. Hunter">Duncan Hunter</a> became a major proponent of border fencing in the San Diego sector; surplus <a href="/wiki/Marston_Mat" title="Marston Mat">military landing mats</a> were obtained to use as an initial border fence.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Stadium lighting, ground sensors and infra-red cameras were also placed in the area.  Eventually the primitive landing mat fence was replaced with a modern triple fence line<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> that begins over one hundred yards into the Pacific Ocean at Imperial Beach, CA and ends more than 13 miles (19&#160;km) inland on Otay Mesa where the mountains begin.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_border">Northern border</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Northern border">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USBP_snow_M14_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/USBP_snow_M14_2017.jpg/220px-USBP_snow_M14_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/USBP_snow_M14_2017.jpg/330px-USBP_snow_M14_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/USBP_snow_M14_2017.jpg/440px-USBP_snow_M14_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5312" data-file-height="2988" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USBP_snow_M14_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An agent armed with an <a href="/wiki/M14_rifle" title="M14 rifle">M14 rifle</a> tracking someone in harsh winter conditions on the northern border.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Border_Patrol_at_Canadian_border_in_Beebe_Plain,_Vermont.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Border_Patrol_at_Canadian_border_in_Beebe_Plain%2C_Vermont.jpg/220px-Border_Patrol_at_Canadian_border_in_Beebe_Plain%2C_Vermont.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Border_Patrol_at_Canadian_border_in_Beebe_Plain%2C_Vermont.jpg/330px-Border_Patrol_at_Canadian_border_in_Beebe_Plain%2C_Vermont.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Border_Patrol_at_Canadian_border_in_Beebe_Plain%2C_Vermont.jpg/440px-Border_Patrol_at_Canadian_border_in_Beebe_Plain%2C_Vermont.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Border_Patrol_at_Canadian_border_in_Beebe_Plain,_Vermont.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Border crossing to Canada at <a href="/wiki/Beebe_Plain,_Vermont" title="Beebe Plain, Vermont">Beebe Plain, Vermont</a></div></div></div>
<p>Through agency <a href="/wiki/Whistleblower_Protection_Act" title="Whistleblower Protection Act">whistleblowers</a>, Agent Mark Hall and Agent Robert Lindemann, it was revealed that in 2001, the Border Patrol had approximately 324 agents assigned along the <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Canada–United States border">Canada–United States border</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Northern border staffing had been increased by 1,128 agents to 1,470 agents by the end of fiscal year 2008, and is projected to expand to 1,845 by the end of fiscal year 2009, a sixfold increase. Resources that support Border Patrol agents include the use of new technology and a more focused application of air and marine assets.
</p><p>The northern border sectors are (west to east): Blaine (Washington), Spokane (Washington), Havre (Montana), Grand Forks (North Dakota), Detroit (Selfridge ANGB, Michigan), Buffalo (New York), Swanton (Vermont), and Houlton (Maine).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_new_strategy">The new strategy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The new strategy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Mexico_border_surveillance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/US_Mexico_border_surveillance.jpg/220px-US_Mexico_border_surveillance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/US_Mexico_border_surveillance.jpg/330px-US_Mexico_border_surveillance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/US_Mexico_border_surveillance.jpg/440px-US_Mexico_border_surveillance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1936" data-file-height="2106" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Mexico_border_surveillance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cameras add "Smart Border" surveillance.</div></div></div>
<p>In November 2005, the U.S. Border Patrol published an updated national strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The goal of this updated strategy is operational control of the United States border.  The strategy has five main objectives:
</p>
<ol><li>Apprehend terrorists and terrorist weapons illegally entering the United States;</li>
<li>Deter illegal entries through improved enforcement;</li>
<li>Detect, apprehend, and deter smugglers of humans, drugs, and other contraband;</li>
<li>Use "smart border" technology; and</li>
<li>Reduce crime in border communities, improving quality of life.</li></ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Capabilities">Capabilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Capabilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MQ-9_Reaper_CBP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/MQ-9_Reaper_CBP.jpg/220px-MQ-9_Reaper_CBP.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="101" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/MQ-9_Reaper_CBP.jpg/330px-MQ-9_Reaper_CBP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/MQ-9_Reaper_CBP.jpg/440px-MQ-9_Reaper_CBP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="346" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MQ-9_Reaper_CBP.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/General_Atomics_MQ-9_Reaper" title="General Atomics MQ-9 Reaper">MQ-9 Predator B</a> UAS operated by United States Customs and Border Protection</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Border_Patrol_ATV_IMG_5278.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Border_Patrol_ATV_IMG_5278.jpg/220px-Border_Patrol_ATV_IMG_5278.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Border_Patrol_ATV_IMG_5278.jpg/330px-Border_Patrol_ATV_IMG_5278.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Border_Patrol_ATV_IMG_5278.jpg/440px-Border_Patrol_ATV_IMG_5278.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Border_Patrol_ATV_IMG_5278.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Border Patrol all-terrain vehicles</div></div></div>
<p>The United States border is a barely discernible line in uninhabited deserts, canyons, or mountains. The Border Patrol utilizes a variety of equipment and methods, such as electronic sensors placed at strategic locations along the border, to detect people or vehicles entering the country illegally. Video monitors and night vision scopes are also used to detect illegal entries. Agents patrol the border in vehicles, boats, aircraft, and afoot. In some areas, the Border Patrol employs horses, all-terrain motorcycles, bicycles, and snowmobiles. Air surveillance capabilities are provided by <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">unmanned aerial vehicles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The primary activity of a Border Patrol Agent is "Line Watch". Line Watch involves the detection, prevention, and apprehension of terrorists, illegal aliens and smugglers of aliens at or near the land border by maintaining surveillance from a covert position; following up on leads; responding to electronic sensor, television systems and aircraft sightings; and interpreting and following tracks, marks, and other physical evidence. Major activities include traffic check, traffic observation, city patrol, transportation check, administrative, intelligence, and anti-smuggling activities.<sup id="cite_ref-who_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Traffic checks are conducted on major highways leading away from the border to detect and apprehend illegal aliens attempting to travel further into the interior of the United States after evading detection at the border, and to detect illegal narcotics.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Transportation checks are inspections of interior-bound conveyances, which include buses, commercial aircraft, passenger and freight trains, and marine craft.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Marine Patrols are conducted along the coastal waterways of the United States, primarily along the Pacific coast, the Caribbean, the tip of Florida, and Puerto Rico and interior waterways common to the United States and Canada. Border Patrol conducts border control activities from 130 marine craft of various sizes. The Border Patrol maintains watercraft ranging from blue-water craft to inflatable-hull craft, in 16 sectors, in addition to headquarters special operations components.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Horse and bike patrols are used to augment regular vehicle and foot patrols. Horse units patrol remote areas along the international boundary that are inaccessible to standard all-terrain vehicles. Bike patrol aids city patrol and is used over rough terrain to support linewatch.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Snowmobiles are used to patrol remote areas along the northern border in the winter.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion">Expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Detroit_-_Inside_Greyhound_Bus_Station_-_P1080197.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Detroit_-_Inside_Greyhound_Bus_Station_-_P1080197.JPG/220px-Detroit_-_Inside_Greyhound_Bus_Station_-_P1080197.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Detroit_-_Inside_Greyhound_Bus_Station_-_P1080197.JPG/330px-Detroit_-_Inside_Greyhound_Bus_Station_-_P1080197.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Detroit_-_Inside_Greyhound_Bus_Station_-_P1080197.JPG/440px-Detroit_-_Inside_Greyhound_Bus_Station_-_P1080197.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Detroit_-_Inside_Greyhound_Bus_Station_-_P1080197.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Border Patrol Agents at the <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">Greyhound</a> bus station in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit, Michigan</a> in February 2011. Immigration checks on trains, buses, and highways within 100 miles of the northern border have become more common.<sup id="cite_ref-COE2011_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COE2011-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div> 
<p>In 1992, the United States Border Patrol had approximately 4,139 Patrol Agents on the job.  Attrition in the Border Patrol was normally at 5%.  From 1995–2001 annual attrition rose to above 10%, which was a period when the Border Patrol was undergoing massive hiring.  In 2002 the attrition rate climbed to 18%.  The 18% attrition was largely attributed to agents transferring to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Air_Marshals" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Air Marshals">Federal Air Marshals</a> after <a href="/wiki/9/11" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11">9/11</a>. Since that time the attrition rate has decreased. Congress increased journeyman Border Patrol Agent pay from a <a href="/wiki/General_Schedule_(US_civil_service_pay_scale)" title="General Schedule (US civil service pay scale)">GS-9 rate to a GS-11 rate</a> in 2002.   The Border Patrol Marine Position was created in 2009 (BPA-M).
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_Reform_and_Terrorism_Prevention_Act" title="Intelligence Reform and Terrorism Prevention Act">Intelligence Reform and Terrorism Prevention Act</a> of 2004 (signed by President Bush on December 17, 2004) authorized hiring an additional 10,000 agents, "subject to appropriation". This authorization nearly doubled the Border Patrol manpower from 11,000 to 20,000 agents by 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> As of 2016, roughly half of the agents are <a href="/wiki/Latino_Americans" class="mw-redirect" title="Latino Americans">Latino Americans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Secure_Fence_Act_of_2006" title="Secure Fence Act of 2006">Secure Fence Act</a>, signed by President George W. Bush on October 26, 2006, has met with much opposition. In October 2007, environmental groups and concerned citizens filed a restraining order hoping to halt the construction of the fence, set to be built between the United States and Mexico. The act mandates that the fence be built by December 2008. Ultimately, the United States seeks to put fencing around the 1,945-mile (3,130&#160;km) border, but the act requires only 700 miles (1,100&#160;km) of fencing. DHS secretary Michael Chertoff has bypassed environmental and other oppositions with a waiver that was granted to him by Congress in Section 102 of the act, which allows DHS to avoid any conflicts that would prevent a speedy assembly of the fence.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This action has led many environment groups and landowners to speak out against the impending construction of the fence.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Environment and wildlife groups fear that the plans to clear brush, construct fences, install bright lights, motion sensors, and cameras will scare wildlife and endanger the indigenous species of the area.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Environmentalists claim that the ecosystem could be affected because a border fence would restrict movement of all animal species, which in turn would keep them from water and food sources on one side or another. Desert plants would also feel the impact, as they would be uprooted in many areas where the fence is set to occupy.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, property owners in these areas feared a loss of land.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(geographic_names)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)"><span title="The geographic scope near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2019)">where?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Landowners would have had to give some of their land over to the government for the fence. Brownsville mayor Pat Ahumada favored alternative options to a border fence. He suggested that the Rio Grande be widened and deepened to provide for a natural barrier to hinder illegal aliens and drug smugglers.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_Operations_Group">Special Operations Group</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Special Operations Group">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USBP-SRT-New_Orleans.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/USBP-SRT-New_Orleans.jpg/220px-USBP-SRT-New_Orleans.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/USBP-SRT-New_Orleans.jpg/330px-USBP-SRT-New_Orleans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/USBP-SRT-New_Orleans.jpg/440px-USBP-SRT-New_Orleans.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4992" data-file-height="3328" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USBP-SRT-New_Orleans.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Border Patrol agents—including the Border Patrol Tactical Unit (BORTAC) and Laredo Sector Special Response Team—conduct a room-by-room search of a New Orleans hotel following <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Border_Patrol_Tactical_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Border Patrol Tactical Unit">Border Patrol Tactical Unit</a> (BORTAC)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Border_Patrol,_Search,_Trauma_and_Rescue" title="Border Patrol, Search, Trauma and Rescue">Border Patrol, Search, Trauma and Rescue</a> (BORSTAR)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mobile_Response_Team&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mobile Response Team (page does not exist)">Mobile Response Team</a> (MRT)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_specialized_programs">Other specialized programs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other specialized programs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CBT_Canine_Enforcement_Program.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/CBT_Canine_Enforcement_Program.jpg/150px-CBT_Canine_Enforcement_Program.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/CBT_Canine_Enforcement_Program.jpg/225px-CBT_Canine_Enforcement_Program.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/CBT_Canine_Enforcement_Program.jpg/300px-CBT_Canine_Enforcement_Program.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1360" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CBT_Canine_Enforcement_Program.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>BORSTAR canine team conducting rappeling training</div></div></div>
<p>In 2007, the U.S. Border Patrol created the Special Operations Group (SOG) headquartered in El Paso, Texas, to coordinate the special operations units of the agency.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
The U.S. Border Patrol has a number of other specialized programs and details. Marine Patrol – In the <a href="/wiki/Riverine" class="mw-redirect" title="Riverine">riverine</a> environments of the northern and southwestern borders of the continental United States, the Border Patrol conducts border control activities from the decks of marine craft of various sizes.  Since 2006, the U.S. Border Patrol has relinquished its <a href="/wiki/Littoral" class="mw-redirect" title="Littoral">littoral</a> law enforcement missions in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Territorial_seas" class="mw-redirect" title="Territorial seas">territorial seas</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Air_and_Marine" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of Air and Marine">Office of Air and Marine</a>.  The U.S. Border Patrol maintains over 130 vessels, ranging from blue-water craft to inflatable-hull craft, in 16 sectors, in addition to Headquarters special operations components.</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Border_Patrol_Special_Operations_HQ.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/US_Border_Patrol_Special_Operations_HQ.jpg/220px-US_Border_Patrol_Special_Operations_HQ.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/US_Border_Patrol_Special_Operations_HQ.jpg/330px-US_Border_Patrol_Special_Operations_HQ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/US_Border_Patrol_Special_Operations_HQ.jpg/440px-US_Border_Patrol_Special_Operations_HQ.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1365" data-file-height="1634" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Border_Patrol_Special_Operations_HQ.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sign for U.S. Border Patrol Special Operations Group on <a href="/wiki/Biggs_Army_Airfield" title="Biggs Army Airfield">Biggs Army Airfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Bliss" title="Fort Bliss">Fort Bliss</a>, El Paso, Texas</div></div></div>
<p><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Police_dog" title="Police dog">K9</a> Units, <a href="/wiki/Mounted_police" title="Mounted police">Mounted Patrol</a>, Bike patrol, Sign-cutting (tracking), <a href="/wiki/Snowmobile" title="Snowmobile">Snowmobile</a> unit, Infrared scope unit, <a href="/wiki/Criminal_intelligence" title="Criminal intelligence">Intelligence</a>, <a href="/wiki/People_smuggling" title="People smuggling">Anti-smuggling</a> Investigations Unit (ASU/DISRUPT, Border Criminal Alien Program, Multi-agency Anti-Gang Task Forces (regional &amp; local units), <a href="/wiki/Guard_of_honour" title="Guard of honour">Honor Guard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pipes_and_Drums" class="mw-redirect" title="Pipes and Drums">Pipes and Drums</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chaplain" title="Chaplain">Chaplain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peer_Support" class="mw-redirect" title="Peer Support">Peer Support</a>, Mobile Surveillance Unit.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lifesaving">Lifesaving</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Lifesaving">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CBP_Rescue_Beacon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/CBP_Rescue_Beacon.jpg/170px-CBP_Rescue_Beacon.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/CBP_Rescue_Beacon.jpg/255px-CBP_Rescue_Beacon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/CBP_Rescue_Beacon.jpg/340px-CBP_Rescue_Beacon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CBP_Rescue_Beacon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This rescue beacon states in English and Spanish: "Attention: You Cannot Walk To Safety From This Point! You Are In Danger of Dying If You Do Not Summon Help! If You Need Help, Push Red Button, U.S. Border Patrol Will Arrive in One Hour, Do Not Leave This Location"</div></div></div>
<p>"Operation Gatekeeper" was launched in 1994 to stop aliens from crossing illegally into the United States.  The strategy included increased enforcement and extensive fencing near border cities, with the twofold purpose of deflecting aliens to remote areas where they could more easily be detected and apprehended, as well as using the formidable mountains, deserts, and <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a> as a deterrent to easy passage.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>  The newly erected <a href="/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_barrier" title="Mexico–United States barrier">Mexico–United States barrier</a>—which at some remote locations is no more than a fence—has also forced aliens and human traffickers to seek out remote desert locations in California, Arizona, New Mexico and Texas where they may attempt crossing.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The "funnel effect" created by both these strategies has contributed to the <a href="/wiki/Migrant_deaths_along_the_Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Migrant deaths along the Mexico–United States border">deaths</a> of thousands of aliens, whose remains are often found in the hot desert or freezing mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As early as 1998, the former <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Naturalization_Service" title="Immigration and Naturalization Service">Immigration and Naturalization Service</a> implemented the Border Safety Initiative in response to concerns about the number of aliens injured or killed while attempting to cross the border. It was noted that Border Patrol agents routinely supplied water, food, and medical care to aliens.<sup id="cite_ref-GAO_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GAO-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> That same year, <a href="/wiki/Border_Patrol,_Search,_Trauma_and_Rescue" title="Border Patrol, Search, Trauma and Rescue">Border Patrol, Search, Trauma and Rescue</a> (BORSTAR), a specialized unit trained in emergency search and rescue, was established with the purpose of assisting injured or stranded aliens at remote locations.<sup id="cite_ref-BP-A_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BP-A-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2002, the first "rescue beacons" were installed in desert areas considered especially dangerous.<sup id="cite_ref-Polliard_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Polliard-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The beacons are solar powered and highly visible, and have a button which alerts Border Patrol agents by radio signal, after which a helicopter or ground unit is dispatched.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/Bill_Frist" title="Bill Frist">Bill Frist</a> commented in 2006: "these beacons, I believe, are an absolutely vital link in our border security system... We know that beacons work: CBP has already saved dozens of people based entirely on beacon alerts."<sup id="cite_ref-Polliard_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Polliard-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The Border Patrol frequently publishes reports about stranded and injured individuals rescued at beacon locations.
</p><p>During a 12-month period in 2011–12, Border Patrol agents made 1,312 rescues along the Mexico-United States border, nearly half occurring in the Tucson Sector.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Border_Patrol_Sectors">Border Patrol Sectors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Border Patrol Sectors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CBP_Sectors_Map.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/CBP_Sectors_Map.jpg/220px-CBP_Sectors_Map.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/CBP_Sectors_Map.jpg/330px-CBP_Sectors_Map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/CBP_Sectors_Map.jpg/440px-CBP_Sectors_Map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1023" data-file-height="681" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CBP_Sectors_Map.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Border Patrol sectors</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Border_Patrol_Holding_Rooms,_Fort_Brown_Station,_Brownsville,_Texas_(2014).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/U.S._Border_Patrol_Holding_Rooms%2C_Fort_Brown_Station%2C_Brownsville%2C_Texas_%282014%29.jpg/220px-U.S._Border_Patrol_Holding_Rooms%2C_Fort_Brown_Station%2C_Brownsville%2C_Texas_%282014%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/U.S._Border_Patrol_Holding_Rooms%2C_Fort_Brown_Station%2C_Brownsville%2C_Texas_%282014%29.jpg/330px-U.S._Border_Patrol_Holding_Rooms%2C_Fort_Brown_Station%2C_Brownsville%2C_Texas_%282014%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/U.S._Border_Patrol_Holding_Rooms%2C_Fort_Brown_Station%2C_Brownsville%2C_Texas_%282014%29.jpg/440px-U.S._Border_Patrol_Holding_Rooms%2C_Fort_Brown_Station%2C_Brownsville%2C_Texas_%282014%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="727" data-file-height="542" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Border_Patrol_Holding_Rooms,_Fort_Brown_Station,_Brownsville,_Texas_(2014).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Holding room at Fort Brown Station, <a href="/wiki/Brownsville,_Texas" title="Brownsville, Texas">Brownsville, Texas</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Border_Patrol_in_Montana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Border_Patrol_in_Montana.jpg/220px-Border_Patrol_in_Montana.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Border_Patrol_in_Montana.jpg/330px-Border_Patrol_in_Montana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Border_Patrol_in_Montana.jpg/440px-Border_Patrol_in_Montana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2433" data-file-height="1622" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Border_Patrol_in_Montana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Border Patrol in Montana.</div></div></div>
<p>There are 20 Border Patrol sectors, each headed by a Sector Chief Patrol Agent.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Training">Training</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Training">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>All Border Patrol agents spend a minimum of 26 weeks at the Border Patrol Academy in <a href="/wiki/Artesia,_New_Mexico" title="Artesia, New Mexico">Artesia, New Mexico</a>, which is a component of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Law_Enforcement_Training_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Law Enforcement Training Center">Federal Law Enforcement Training Center</a> (FLETC).   Border Patrol Agent Trainees are instructed in courses including; Spanish, criminal law, nationality law, and administrative immigration law, police sciences, self-defense and arrest techniques, firearms training with pistol, shotgun and rifle, police vehicle driving, and other Border Patrol / federal law enforcement subjects.
</p><p>Once they arrive back at their duty station, Trainees then must graduate from the Field Training Officer (FTO) program, an on-the-job training program, which varies in length from a minimum of 12 weeks to a maximum of over 16 weeks long, depending on the practical demands of the duty station and local management.  They must also successfully complete the Post Academy Training Program, an extension of the Border Patrol Academy where Trainees complete additional classroom-based training over the course of their first nine months back at their duty station.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearance">Appearance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Appearance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniforms">Uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Border Patrol, c. 2007, wore the following types of uniforms:
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CBP_Officers_pay_tribute_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/CBP_Officers_pay_tribute_2007.jpg/220px-CBP_Officers_pay_tribute_2007.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/CBP_Officers_pay_tribute_2007.jpg/330px-CBP_Officers_pay_tribute_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/CBP_Officers_pay_tribute_2007.jpg/440px-CBP_Officers_pay_tribute_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2958" data-file-height="2232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CBP_Officers_pay_tribute_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A color guard composed of CBP officers and USBP agents at a Washington, D.C. ceremony in May 2007.</div></div></div>
<ul><li>Summer Dress uniform – The summer dress uniform consists of a short-sleeve, olive-green dress shirt (which may or may not have blue shoulder straps), brass <a href="/wiki/Nameplate" title="Nameplate">nameplate</a>, badge, olive-green <a href="/wiki/Slacks" class="mw-redirect" title="Slacks">slacks</a> with a blue stripe running the length of the seam, and black dress shoes or dress boots. A green, straw <a href="/wiki/Campaign_hat" title="Campaign hat">campaign hat</a> is worn with this uniform.</li>
<li>Winter Dress uniform – The winter dress uniform consists of a long-sleeve, olive green dress shirt, navy-blue <a href="/wiki/Clip-on_tie" title="Clip-on tie">clip-on tie</a> with a brass <a href="/wiki/Tie_tack" class="mw-redirect" title="Tie tack">tie tack</a>, olive-green <a href="/wiki/Ike_jacket" class="mw-redirect" title="Ike jacket">ike jacket</a> with blue accents (shoulder straps and cuffs), brass nameplate, badge, olive-green slacks with a blue stripe running the length of the seam, and black dress shoes or dress boots. a green, felt <a href="/wiki/Campaign_hat" title="Campaign hat">campaign hat</a> with a black, leather <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hat_band&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hat band (page does not exist)">hat band</a> is worn with this uniform.</li>
<li>Ceremonial Dress uniform – Worn primarily by border patrol <a href="/wiki/Guard_of_honour" title="Guard of honour">honor guard</a> agents, the ceremonial dress uniform is roughly identical to the winter dress uniform, with the exception that a <a href="/wiki/Tunic" title="Tunic">tunic</a> is worn with this uniform, rather than an ike jacket. White, cloth gloves are also worn with this uniform.</li>
<li>Rough duty uniform – The rough duty uniform consists of a green, long-sleeve or short-sleeve work shirt, green <a href="/wiki/Cargo_pants" title="Cargo pants">cargo pants</a>, and black work boots; a green <a href="/wiki/Baseball_cap" title="Baseball cap">baseball cap</a>  or <a href="/wiki/Cowboy_hat" title="Cowboy hat">cowboy hat</a> is typically worn with this uniform.
<ul><li>There are also specialized rough duty uniforms for marine patrol (riverine), northern border cold weather, horse patrol and bike patrol agents.</li></ul></li>
<li>Highland Uniform – Worn by members of the United States Border Patrol Pipes and Drums in the performance of their official duties, this uniform includes a kilt made of the official Border Patrol Tartan, custom made ceremonial coat, glengarry, sporran and spats.</li>
<li>Organization patches – The Border Patrol wears two:
<ul><li>The CBP patch is worn on the right sleeves of the uniform. It contains the DHS seal against a black background with a "keystone" shape. A "keystone" is the central, wedge-shaped stone in an arch, which holds all the other stones in place.</li>
<li>Border Patrol agents retain the circular legacy Border Patrol patch, which is worn on the left sleeve.</li></ul></li></ul>
<p>The Border Patrol uniform is getting its first makeover since the 1950s to appear more like military fatigues and less like a police officer's duty garb.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Leather belts with brass buckles are being replaced by nylon belts with quick-release plastic buckles, slacks are being replaced by lightweight cargo pants, and shiny badges and nameplates are being replaced by cloth patches.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newton-Azrak_Award_for_Heroism">Newton-Azrak Award for Heroism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Newton-Azrak Award for Heroism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Border Patrol's highest honor is the Newton-Azrak Award for Heroism.  This Award is bestowed to Border Patrol Agents for extraordinary actions, service; accomplishments reflecting unusual courage or bravery in the line of duty; or an extraordinarily heroic or humane act committed during times of extreme stress or in an emergency.
</p><p>This award is named for Border Patrol Inspectors Theodore Newton<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> and George Azrak,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> who were murdered by two drug smugglers in San Diego County in 1967.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Equipment">Equipment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Equipment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Weapons">Weapons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Weapons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CBP_M14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/CBP_M14.jpg/170px-CBP_M14.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/CBP_M14.jpg/255px-CBP_M14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/CBP_M14.jpg/340px-CBP_M14.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2199" data-file-height="3246" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CBP_M14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Border Patrol Honor Guard Agent carrying an <a href="/wiki/M14_rifle" title="M14 rifle">M14 rifle</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Border Patrol agents are issued the <a href="/wiki/H%26K_P2000" class="mw-redirect" title="H&amp;K P2000">H&amp;K P2000</a> double action LEM (Law Enforcement Modification) pistol in <a href="/wiki/.40_S%26W" title=".40 S&amp;W">.40 S&amp;W</a> caliber. It can contain as many as 13 rounds of ammunition (12 in the magazine and 1 in the chamber). Up until 1994 the Border Patrol issued its Patrol Agents a .357 Magnum revolver as their duty sidearm, a <a href="/wiki/Smith_%26_Wesson" title="Smith &amp; Wesson">Smith &amp; Wesson</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ruger" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruger">Ruger</a> model large frame, six shot revolver.  The Border Patrol preferred this weapon because it did not jam in harsh conditions, like those of the southwestern border, and also because of the strong "<a href="/wiki/Stopping_power" title="Stopping power">stopping power</a>" of the .357 Magnum cartridge. Although up until 1994 Patrol Agents could purchase a weapon from the agency list of approved authorized personal weapons for duty carry. This list included the Glock Models 17 and 19 pistols in 9mm, the <a href="/wiki/SIG_Sauer_P220" title="SIG Sauer P220">SIG Sauer P220</a> pistol in .45 ACP caliber, the <a href="/wiki/Colt_Python" title="Colt Python">Colt Python</a> .357 Magnum revolver, and the <a href="/wiki/Smith_%26_Wesson_Model_19" title="Smith &amp; Wesson Model 19">Smith &amp; Wesson Model 19/66</a> .357 Magnum revolver. The Border Patrol adopted the <a href="/wiki/Beretta_92" title="Beretta 92">Beretta Model 96D</a>, a .40 S&amp;W caliber semi-automatic pistol (modified for Double-Action Only) (with 11-round capacity magazines) as its duty issue sidearm in 1995.  The .40 S&amp;W caliber jacketed hollow-point cartridge was adopted because of its excellent "stopping" power and its superior ballistic characteristics over the 9mm cartridge. In late 2006 the H&amp;K P2000 pistol was adopted as the Border Patrol's primary duty sidearm.  The H&amp;K Model USP Compact pistol, H&amp;K Model P2000SK (sub-compact) and Beretta M96D .40 S&amp;W caliber pistols are authorized as secondary sidearms.
</p><p>On April 9, 2019, CBP announced that the U.S. Border Patrol would transition from the .40 caliber H&amp;K P2000 to an unnamed 9-millimeter Glock pistol, by the end of fiscal year 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>  It has since been revealed that the three <a href="/wiki/Glock" title="Glock">Glock</a> handguns that would be issued to CBP officers and agents would be the model G26, model G19, and the specifically manufactured for CBP model G47.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Border_Patrol_Agent_in_Nogales,_Arizona.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Border_Patrol_Agent_in_Nogales%2C_Arizona.jpg/220px-Border_Patrol_Agent_in_Nogales%2C_Arizona.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Border_Patrol_Agent_in_Nogales%2C_Arizona.jpg/330px-Border_Patrol_Agent_in_Nogales%2C_Arizona.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Border_Patrol_Agent_in_Nogales%2C_Arizona.jpg/440px-Border_Patrol_Agent_in_Nogales%2C_Arizona.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6480" data-file-height="4320" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Border_Patrol_Agent_in_Nogales,_Arizona.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Patrolling a tunnel in <a href="/wiki/Nogales,_Arizona" title="Nogales, Arizona">Nogales, Arizona</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Like many other law enforcement agencies, the 12 <a href="/wiki/Gauge_(bore_diameter)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gauge (bore diameter)">gauge</a> <a href="/wiki/Remington_Model_870" title="Remington Model 870">Remington Model 870</a> is the standard pump-action shotgun. The Border Patrol issue Model 870 has been modified by Scattergun Technologies to Border Patrol specifications including: a 14-inch barrel, a five-shot capacity magazine, a composite stock with pistol grip, and night sights with a tactical "ghost-ring" rear sight. The old Border Patrol "anti-bandit" units used to use a 12-gauge, semi-automatic shotgun with a sawed-off barrel. This weapon had the designated name of a "Sidewinder."  The USBP anti-bandit units were decommissioned in the late 1980s.
</p><p>Border Patrol agents also commonly carry the <a href="/wiki/.223_Remington" title=".223 Remington">.223</a> caliber Colt <a href="/wiki/M4_Carbine" class="mw-redirect" title="M4 Carbine">M4 Carbine (Specifically the updated M4A1)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/H%26K_UMP" class="mw-redirect" title="H&amp;K UMP">H&amp;K UMP</a> .40 caliber <a href="/wiki/Submachine_gun" title="Submachine gun">submachine gun</a>. The <a href="/wiki/.308_Winchester" title=".308 Winchester">.308</a> caliber <a href="/wiki/M14_rifle" title="M14 rifle">M14 rifle</a> is used for ceremonial purposes and by agents who are qualified with the rifle and <a href="/wiki/BORTAC" title="BORTAC">BORTAC</a>.
</p><p>As less than lethal options, the Border Patrol uses the FN 303 Launcher.  The FN 303 fires plastic pellet balls containing OC (Oleoresin Capsicum) Pepper dust.  The plastic pellet balls burst on impact spraying the suspect with OC Pepper dust and also act as an impact projectile. The Border Patrol also issues its agents OC Pepper spray canisters, tasers and a collapsible/telescopic (or telescoping) steel police baton.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection,_Riverine_Unit_Patrols_Rio_Grande_River_Border_in_Air-Boat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection%2C_Riverine_Unit_Patrols_Rio_Grande_River_Border_in_Air-Boat.jpg/220px-U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection%2C_Riverine_Unit_Patrols_Rio_Grande_River_Border_in_Air-Boat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection%2C_Riverine_Unit_Patrols_Rio_Grande_River_Border_in_Air-Boat.jpg/330px-U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection%2C_Riverine_Unit_Patrols_Rio_Grande_River_Border_in_Air-Boat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection%2C_Riverine_Unit_Patrols_Rio_Grande_River_Border_in_Air-Boat.jpg/440px-U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection%2C_Riverine_Unit_Patrols_Rio_Grande_River_Border_in_Air-Boat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6480" data-file-height="4320" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection,_Riverine_Unit_Patrols_Rio_Grande_River_Border_in_Air-Boat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Patrolling the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Airboat" title="Airboat">airboat</a> at <a href="/wiki/Laredo,_Texas" title="Laredo, Texas">Laredo, Texas</a>, 2013.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg/220px-Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg/330px-Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg/440px-Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="539" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Office_of_CBP_Air_and_Marine_helicopter_and_boats.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Helicopter and boats</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Texas,_Border_Patrol_Agents,_McAllen_Horse_Patrol_Unit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/South_Texas%2C_Border_Patrol_Agents%2C_McAllen_Horse_Patrol_Unit.jpg/220px-South_Texas%2C_Border_Patrol_Agents%2C_McAllen_Horse_Patrol_Unit.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/South_Texas%2C_Border_Patrol_Agents%2C_McAllen_Horse_Patrol_Unit.jpg/330px-South_Texas%2C_Border_Patrol_Agents%2C_McAllen_Horse_Patrol_Unit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/South_Texas%2C_Border_Patrol_Agents%2C_McAllen_Horse_Patrol_Unit.jpg/440px-South_Texas%2C_Border_Patrol_Agents%2C_McAllen_Horse_Patrol_Unit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Texas,_Border_Patrol_Agents,_McAllen_Horse_Patrol_Unit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A USBP Horse Patrol in southern Texas.</div></div></div>
<p>Unlike in many other law enforcement agencies in the United States, the Border Patrol operates over 10,000 <a href="/wiki/SUV" class="mw-redirect" title="SUV">SUVs</a> and pickup trucks, which are known for their capabilities to move around in any sort of terrain. These vehicles may have individual revolving lights (strobes or LEDs) and/or light bars and sirens and/or have their bumpers removed or have off-road suspension and tires. An extensive modernization drive has ensured that these vehicles are equipped with wireless sets in communication with a central control room. Border Patrol vehicles may also have equipment such as emergency first aid kits. Some sectors make use of sedans like the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Crown_Victoria_Police_Interceptor" title="Ford Crown Victoria Police Interceptor">Ford Crown Victoria Police Interceptor</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Dodge_Charger_(LX)#Police_package_version" class="mw-redirect" title="Dodge Charger (LX)">Dodge Charger</a> as patrol cars or high speed "interceptors" on highways. The U.S. Border Patrol has approximately 2,000 sedans. The Border Patrol also operates all-terrain vehicles, motorcycles, snowmobiles, and small boats in riverine environments.
</p><p>In 2005, all Border Patrol and ICE aircraft operations were combined under CBP's <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Air_and_Marine" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of Air and Marine">Office of Air and Marine</a>.  All CBP vessel operations within the Customs Waters and on the high seas are conducted by Marine Interdiction Agents of the Office of Air and Marine.
</p><p>Color schemes of Border Patrol vehicles are either a long green stripe running the length of the vehicle (older vehicles) or a broad green diagonal stripe (newer vehicles) on the door. Most Border Patrol vehicles are painted predominantly white. During the 1960s to mid-1980s Border Patrol vehicles were painted a light green.
</p><p>The Border Patrol also extensively uses horses for remote area patrols. As of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the U.S. Border Patrol has 205 horses. Most are employed along the <a href="/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Mexico–United States border">Mexico–United States border</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, these animals are fed special processed feed pellets so that their wastes do not spread non-native plants in the national parks and wildlife areas they patrol.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Killed_in_the_line_of_duty">Killed in the line of duty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Killed in the line of duty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since 1904, the Border Patrol has lost 123 officers in the line of duty, more than any other federal law enforcement agency during that time period.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
