<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_incursions">Armed incursions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Armed incursions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On August 7, 2008, <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Army" title="Mexican Army">Mexican troops</a> crossed the border into Arizona and held a U.S. Border Patrol Agent at gunpoint. Agents stationed at <a href="/wiki/Ajo,_Arizona" title="Ajo, Arizona">Ajo, Arizona</a> said that the Mexican soldiers crossed the border into an isolated area southwest of Tucson and pointed rifles at the agent, who has not been identified. The Mexicans withdrew after other U.S. agents arrived on the scene.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>On March 14, 2000, 16 Mexican soldiers in two humvees chased a Border Patrol agent near Santa Teresa, New Mexico, while another agent came under gunfire. Backup arrived and the soldiers were detained. The Mexican government said the soldiers got lost. The U.S. State Department ordered them sent back to Mexico along with their weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_threats">Death threats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Death threats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Testifying in front of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a>, Border Patrol Chief <a href="/wiki/Mark_Morgan_(law_enforcement_officer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mark Morgan (law enforcement officer)">Mark Morgan</a> said that the Border Patrol is the one of the most assaulted law enforcement agencies;<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> since 2006, over seven thousand agents of the Border Patrol were attacked.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> On numerous occasions USBP agents have been fired upon from the Mexican side of the international border.  Intelligence gathering has discovered bounties being placed on Patrol Agents to be paid by criminal smuggling organizations upon the confirmed murder or kidnapping of a U.S. Border Patrol Agent. In 2008, intelligence learned of a two-million-dollar contract for the murder of a Border Patrol Agent. In 2009 Border Patrol Agent Rosas was murdered in an ambush while on patrol; a bounty may have been paid to the assassins.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms">Criticisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Criticisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>See also:</i> <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_United_States_government#Criticism_of_agencies" title="Criticism of the United States government">Criticism of the United States government § Criticism of agencies</a>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ramos_and_Compean">Ramos and Compean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ramos and Compean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2005, Border Patrol Agents <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Ramos" title="Ignacio Ramos">Ignacio Ramos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jose_Compean" title="Jose Compean">Jose Compean</a> were involved in an incident while pursuing a van in <a href="/wiki/Fabens,_Texas" title="Fabens, Texas">Fabens, Texas</a>. The driver, later identified as Aldrete Davila, was shot by Agent Ramos during a scuffle. Davila escaped back into Mexico, and the agents discovered that the van contained a million dollars worth of marijuana (about 750 pounds). None of the agents at the scene orally reported the shooting, including two supervisors: Robert Arnold, first-line Supervisor and Jonathan Richards, a higher ranking Field Operations Supervisor.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
Ramos and Compean were charged with multiple crimes. Ramos was convicted of causing serious bodily injury, assault with a deadly weapon, discharge of a firearm in relation to a crime of violence, and a civil rights violation.<sup id="cite_ref-Seper_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seper-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Compeán was found <a href="/wiki/Guilty_(law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Guilty (law)">guilty</a> on 11 counts, including discharging a <a href="/wiki/Firearm" title="Firearm">firearm</a> during the commission of a <a href="/wiki/Violent_crime" title="Violent crime">violent crime</a>, which by itself carries a federally mandated 10-year <a href="/wiki/Minimum_sentence" class="mw-redirect" title="Minimum sentence">minimum sentence</a>. Without that charge, both agents involved would have received far shorter sentences. Ramos was sentenced to 11 years and a day in prison and Compean to 12 years.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Jonathan Richards was promoted to the Patrol Agent in Charge of the Santa Teresa, New Mexico Border Patrol Station soon after the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On January 19, 2009, President Bush commuted the sentences of both Ramos and Compean, effectively ending their prison term on March 20, 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> and they were released on February 17, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The case generated widely differing opinion among various commentators and advocacy groups: civil libertarians asserted the agents used illegal and excessive force, while advocates of tighter border control defended the agents actions.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Sergio_Hernandez">Death of Sergio Hernandez</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Death of Sergio Hernandez">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sergio Adrian Hernandez was a teenager who was shot once and killed on June 7, 2010 by Border Patrol agents under a bridge crossing between <a href="/wiki/El_Paso,_Texas" title="El Paso, Texas">El Paso, Texas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Ciudad Juárez">Juarez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tsun_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsun-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Border Patrol agents claimed that there was a mob that was throwing stones at them.<sup id="cite_ref-tsun_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsun-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> They also claimed that Hernandez was trying to cross the U.S. border and that he had already tried to do so in the past<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. For his involvement in the incident, Border Patrol agent Jesus Mesa, Jr. invoked qualified official immunity in his defense.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 10 the Mexican president <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Calder%C3%B3n" title="Felipe Calderón">Felipe Calderón</a> called on the United States to launch a "thorough, impartial" probe into the deaths of two Mexican nationals, including the 14-year-old Hernandez, at the hands of U.S. border police: <i>"I demand the United States government conduct a thorough, impartial ... investigation, concluding with an establishment of the facts and punishment of the culprits."</i><sup id="cite_ref-smh_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smh-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 12, 2010 the television network <a href="/wiki/Univision" title="Univision">Univision</a> aired cellphone video footage of the incident, after which Mexican legislators called for the extradition of the officer accused of the shooting.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Death_of_Anastasio_Hern.C3.A1ndez-Rojas"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Anastasio_Hernández-Rojas">Death of Anastasio Hernández-Rojas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Death of Anastasio Hernández-Rojas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Anastasio_Hern%C3%A1ndez-Rojas" title="Death of Anastasio Hernández-Rojas">Death of Anastasio Hernández-Rojas</a></div>
<p>On May 30, 2010 <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Anastasio_Hern%C3%A1ndez-Rojas" title="Death of Anastasio Hernández-Rojas">Anastasio Hernandez-Rojas</a> died of a heart attack while in the custody of United States Border Patrol (USBP), Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE), and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection" title="U.S. Customs and Border Protection">U.S. Customs and Border Protection</a> (CBP) and agents and officers at the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego%E2%80%93Tijuana" title="San Diego–Tijuana">San Diego–Tijuana</a> border<sup id="cite_ref-SDUnion-Tribune_2017_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDUnion-Tribune_2017-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DOJ_2015_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOJ_2015-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> He was beaten and then shocked by <a href="/wiki/Taser" title="Taser">Tasers</a> on at the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego%E2%80%93Tijuana" title="San Diego–Tijuana">San Diego–Tijuana</a> border<sup id="cite_ref-SDUnion-Tribune_2017_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDUnion-Tribune_2017-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DOJ_2015_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOJ_2015-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> within view of many bystanders with cameras on the busy pedestrian bridge at the <a href="/wiki/San_Ysidro_Port_of_Entry" title="San Ysidro Port of Entry">San Ysidro Port of Entry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SDUnion-Tribune_2017_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDUnion-Tribune_2017-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Although the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> (DOJ) investigation concluded on November 6, 2015 that Hernández Rojas died of a heart attack, an offer of a million-dollar settlement was made to his family.<sup id="cite_ref-DOJ_2015_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOJ_2015-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> None of the agents or officers involved were fired or disciplined for excessive use of force.<sup id="cite_ref-DOJ_2015_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOJ_2015-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In February 2017, his common-law wife and five children accepted the settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-WP_2017_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP_2017_-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Hernández-Rojas's death was profiled in a 2012 <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a> report called <i>Crossing the Line</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Meyer_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meyer-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Nonny_de_la_Pe%C3%B1a" title="Nonny de la Peña">Nonny de la Peña</a>'s, 2013 five-minute-long <a href="/wiki/Virtual_reality" title="Virtual reality">virtual reality</a> called <i>Use of Force</i><sup id="cite_ref-fastcocreate_2013_Hernández_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fastcocreate_2013_Hernández-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> and in a 2014 <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_Liberties_Union" title="American Civil Liberties Union">American Civil Liberties Union</a> report.<sup id="cite_ref-ACLU_2014_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACLU_2014-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Jose_Antonio_Elena_Rodriguez">Death of Jose Antonio Elena Rodriguez</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Death of Jose Antonio Elena Rodriguez">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Killing_of_Jose_Rodriguez" class="mw-redirect" title="Killing of Jose Rodriguez">Killing of Jose Rodriguez</a></div>
<p>As the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wola.org/">Washington Office on Latin America</a>'s <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://borderfactcheck.tumblr.com/post/33715644831/is-firing-bullets-at-rock-throwers-a-justified-use-of">Border Fact Check site</a> points out, a similar incident occurred in October 2012 when 16-year-old Jose Antonio Elena Rodriguez was killed in downtown Nogales, Mexico when a Border Patrol Agent, Lonnie Swartz, opened fire at a group of people allegedly throwing rocks at him; Rodriguez was shot seven times in the back. WOLA and other human rights organizations assert that "...[L]aw enforcement experience offers a series of non-lethal responses to rock throwing incidents along the U.S.-Mexico border," such as pepper ball launchers.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In September 2015, Swartz was indicted on the charge of second-degree murder.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_involving_use_of_tear_gas_and_pepper_spray">Incidents involving use of tear gas and pepper spray</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Incidents involving use of tear gas and pepper spray">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 25, 2013, the San Diego Tribune reported that 100 aliens who tried to cross the border illegally near the San Ysidro port were pepper-sprayed and tear-gassed after throwing bottles and rocks at border patrol agents.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> A similar incident was reported in November 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_abuse">Allegations of abuse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Allegations of abuse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Various civil society and human rights organizations have alleged that abuses of aliens by Border Patrol agents occur frequently:
</p>
<ul><li>June 7, 2018: On a bus travelling from Bakersfield to Las Vegas, agents from the United States Border Patrol stopped and boarded a Greyhound bus at an agricultural checkpoint near the Nevada State Line.  The United States Border Patrol agents had no authorization to stop the Greyhound bus or interrogate passengers since the location was not within the 100 air mile zone of the United States Border.  A passenger recognized that the agents of the United States Border Patrol had violated human rights by conducting their interrogations while lacking authorization.  All other passengers aboard the Greyhound bus were notified that United States Border Patrol agents were not supposed to be stopping the bus or conducting interrogations. After a short argument with the passenger who alerted everybody, the United States Border Patrol agents left the bus.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>  Later, the passenger who had argued with the United States Border Patrol agents decided to post an online petition on <a href="/wiki/Change.org" title="Change.org">Change.org</a> titled "Greyhound: Stop endangering migrants" as a warning for passengers against unauthorised searches by agents of DHS, ICE, and United States Border Patrol.  The online petition has gathered over 60,934 signatures worldwide.</li>
<li>Between 2010 and 2011 alleged excessive use of force by Border Patrol and Field Operations agents led to the death of six Mexican citizens. A PBS report, <i>Crossing the Line</i>, released in July 2012, profiled the case of Hernández-Rojas who died after being beaten and while in custody of the USBP, ICE, and CBP in May 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Meyer_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meyer-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DOJ_2015_70-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOJ_2015-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, in a letter to President Obama posted on the website of the Washington Office on Latin America, 118 civil society organizations criticized the Border Patrol for failing to thoroughly investigate the incident and stated that the Border Patrol "is operating with very little transparency and virtual impunity, especially in the southern border region where Border Patrol and other CBP agents regularly violate the human and civil rights of those who call the border region home."<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>From 2008–2011, the Arizona organization <a href="/wiki/No_More_Deaths" title="No More Deaths">No More Deaths</a> interviewed nearly 13,000 illegal aliens who had been in Border Patrol custody, in the Arizona border towns of Naco, Nogales, and Agua Prieta. Their report, <i>A Culture of Cruelty</i>, documents alleged abuses including denial of or insufficient water and food; failure to provide medical treatment; verbal, physical and psychological abuse; separation of family members and dangerous repatriation practices. In February 2012, Border Patrol Chief Michael Fisher stated in congressional testimony that the Border Patrol takes allegations of abuse seriously.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> However, No More Deaths testified before the Inter-American Commission of Human Rights in March 2012 and stated that in spite of raising their concerns for several years, "the agency has taken the position that such abuses simply do not occur."<sup id="cite_ref-Meyer_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meyer-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>There are allegations of abuse by the United States Border Patrol such as the ones reported by Jesus A. Trevino, that concludes in an article published in the <i>Houston Journal of International Law</i> (2006) with a request to create an independent review commission to oversee the actions of the Border Patrol, and that creating such review board will make the American public aware of the "serious problem of abuse that exists at the border by making this review process public" and that "illegal immigrants deserve the same constitutionally-mandated humane treatment of citizens and legal residents".<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1998, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> investigated allegations of ill-treatment and brutality by officers of the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Naturalization_Service" title="Immigration and Naturalization Service">Immigration and Naturalization Service</a>, and particularly the Border Patrol. Their report said they found indications of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> violations during 1996, 1997 and early 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>An article in <i>Social Justice</i> by Michael Huspek, Leticia Jimenez, Roberto Martinez (1998) cites that in December 1997, John Case, head of the INS Office of Internal Audit, announced at a press conference that public complaints to the INS had risen 29% from 1996, with the "vast majority" of complaints emanating from the southwest border region, but that of the 2,300 cases, the 243 cases of serious allegations of abuse were down in 1997. These serious cases are considered to be distinct from less serious complaints, such as "verbal abuse, discrimination, extended detention without cause."<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p><br />
Incidences of corruption in the U.S. Border Patrol include:
</p>
<ul><li>U.S. Customs and Border Protection gave Accenture Federal Services a $297 million contract in 2017 to hire 7,500 people over five years. An audit by the Department of Homeland Security found that, as of Oct. 1, 2018, Accenture had already been paid $13.6 million but had only hired two people.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Pablo Sergio Barry, an agent charged with one count of harboring an illegal alien (8 U.S.C. § 1324),<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> three counts of false statements, and two counts of making a false document.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> He pleaded guilty.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Christopher E. Bernis, an agent indicted on a charge of harboring an illegal alien for nine months while employed as a U.S. Border Patrol Agent.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Jose De Jesus Ruiz, an agent whose <a href="/wiki/Girlfriend" title="Girlfriend">girlfriend</a> was an illegal alien. He was put on administrative leave pending an investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Oscar Antonio Ortiz, an illegal alien<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> who used a fake <a href="/wiki/Birth_certificate" title="Birth certificate">birth certificate</a> to get into the Border Patrol. He admitted to smuggling more than 100 illegal aliens into the U.S., some of them in his government truck.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> He was charged with conspiring with another agent to smuggle aliens.</li>
<li>An unidentified patrol agent who was recorded on a <a href="/wiki/Telephone_tapping" title="Telephone tapping">wiretap</a> stating that he helped to smuggle 30 to 50 aliens at a time.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_Rights_Violations_and_Racial_Profiling_on_Greyhound_Buses">Human Rights Violations and Racial Profiling on Greyhound Buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Human Rights Violations and Racial Profiling on Greyhound Buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At some Greyhound Bus Stations and along certain routes, agents from <a href="/wiki/DHS" class="mw-redirect" title="DHS">DHS</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Immigration_and_Customs_Enforcement" title="U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement">ICE</a>, and United States Border Patrol  have been known to stop and interrogate passengers. While DHS, ICE, and US Border Patrol Agents are legally allowed to interrogate passengers within 100 air miles of the <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_the_United_States" title="Borders of the United States">Borders of the United States</a>, allegations of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_violations" class="mw-redirect" title="Human rights violations">human rights violations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Racial_profiling" title="Racial profiling">racial profiling</a> that have been filed against the agents who have boarded the Greyhound buses and interrogated passengers at bus stations or along routes outside United States border zones.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>According to the ACLU and some legal experts, without a warrant, United States Border Patrol agents need the explicit consent of Greyhound to be on Greyhound property.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>Protesters against <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Bus_Lines" class="mw-redirect" title="Greyhound Bus Lines">Greyhound Bus Lines</a> allowing the DHS and ICE agents to board the buses have posted an online petition titled "GREYHOUND: STOP THROWING PASSENGERS UNDER THE BUS" on the <a href="/wiki/ACLU" class="mw-redirect" title="ACLU">ACLU</a> website which has already gathered 111,895 signatures worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Border_Patrol_Council">National Border Patrol Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: National Border Patrol Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>National Border Patrol Council (NBPC) is the <a href="/wiki/Labor_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor union">labor union</a> which represents over 17,000 Border Patrol agents and support staff. The NBPC was founded on November 1, 1965, and its parent organization is the <a href="/wiki/American_Federation_of_Government_Employees" title="American Federation of Government Employees">American Federation of Government Employees</a>, <a href="/wiki/AFL-CIO" class="mw-redirect" title="AFL-CIO">AFL-CIO</a>. The NBPC's executive committee is staffed by current and retired Border Patrol agents and, along with its constituent locals, employs a staff of a dozen attorneys and field representatives. The NBPC is associated with the Peace Officer Research Association of California Legal Defense Fund|California's Legal Defense Fund.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Border_Patrol_Foundation">Border Patrol Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Border Patrol Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Border Patrol Foundation was founded in 2009 to assist the survivors of agents killed in the line of duty.  The foundation provides financial support to immediate family members, peer family support, and a scholarship to eligible children.  The foundation recognizes community leaders who have supported the families of fallen agents, and supports programs to improve awareness of the risks faced by agents.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chiefs_of_the_Border_Patrol">Chiefs of the Border Patrol</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Chiefs of the Border Patrol">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Books">Books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><i>Border Patrol</i>, by Alvin Edward Moore.</li>
<li><i>Bleeding Borders</i>, by Steve Arthur Timper</li>
<li><i>The Border Patrol</i>, by Deborah Wells Salter.</li>
<li><i>EWI: Entry Without Inspection</i>, by Fortuna Testarona Valiente.</li>
<li><i>Tracks in the Sand: A Tale of the Border Patrol</i>, by Kent E Lundgren.</li>
<li><i>On The Line: Inside the U.S. Border Patrol</i>, by Alex Pacheco and Erich Krauss.</li>
<li><i>Patrolling Chaos: The U.S. Border Patrol in Deep South Texas</i>, by Robert Lee Maril.</li>
<li><i>The U.S. Border Patrol: Guarding the Nation</i>, by Connie Collwell Miller.</li>
<li><i>My Border Patrol Diary: Laredo, Texas</i>, by Dale Squint.</li>
<li><i>Holding the Line: War Stories of the U.S. Border Patrol</i>, by Gerald Schumacher.</li>
<li><i>The Border Patrol Ate My Dust</i>, by Alicia Alarcon, Ethriam Cash Brammer, and Ethriam Cash Brammer de Gonzales.</li>
<li><i>The Border: Exploring the U.S.-Mexican Divide</i>, by <a href="/wiki/David_J._Danelo" title="David J. Danelo">David J. Danelo</a>.</li>
<li><i>Beat The Border: An Insider's Guide to How the U.S. Border Works and How to Beat It</i>, by Ned Beaumont.</li>
<li><i>West of the Moon: A Border Patrol Agent's Tale</i>, by D.B. Prehoda.</li>
<li><i>The Journey: U.S. Border Patrol &amp; the Solution to the Illegal Alien Problem</i>,  by Donald R. Coppock.</li>
<li><i>Border Patrol: With the U.S. Immigration Service on the Mexican boundary, 1910–54</i>, by Clifford Alan Perkins.</li>
<li><i>Border Patrol: How U.S. Agents Protect Our Borders from Illegal Entry</i>, by Carroll B. Colby.</li>
<li><i>In Mortal Danger: The Battle for America's Border and Security</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Tancredo" title="Tom Tancredo">Tom Tancredo</a>.</li>
<li><i>Border Songs</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Lynch_(writer)" title="Jim Lynch (writer)">Jim Lynch</a>.</li>
<li><i>Crossing the Wire</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Will_Hobbs" title="Will Hobbs">Will Hobbs</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><i>Border Patrolman</i>, a 1936 film in which Border Patrolman Bob Wallace, played by <a href="/wiki/George_O%27Brien_(actor)" title="George O&#39;Brien (actor)">George O'Brien</a>, resigns in protest after being humiliated by the spoiled granddaughter of a millionaire.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Border_Patrol_(1943_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Border Patrol (1943 film)">Border Patrol</a></i>, a 1943 film starring <a href="/wiki/William_C._Boyd" title="William C. Boyd">William C. Boyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andy_Clyde" title="Andy Clyde">Andy Clyde</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Reeves" title="George Reeves">George Reeves</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mitchum" title="Robert Mitchum">Robert Mitchum</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Borderline_(1950_film)" title="Borderline (1950 film)">Borderline</a></i>, a 1950 <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">film noir</a> starring <a href="/wiki/Fred_MacMurray" title="Fred MacMurray">Fred MacMurray</a> about drug smuggling across the Mexico-U.S. border.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Border_Patrol_(US_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Border Patrol (US TV series)">Border Patrol</a></i>, a 1959 television series starring <a href="/wiki/Richard_Webb_(actor)" title="Richard Webb (actor)">Richard Webb</a> as the fictitious deputy chief of the U.S. Border Patrol.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Borderline_(1980_film)" title="Borderline (1980 film)">Borderline</a></i>, a 1980 movie starring <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bronson" title="Charles Bronson">Charles Bronson</a> about a Border Patrol Agent in charge of a station located in the hills southeast of San Diego, near the Mexico-U.S. border.  Bronson's character and the agents under his command pursue and apprehend a violent human trafficker/smuggler played by <a href="/wiki/Ed_Harris" title="Ed Harris">Ed Harris</a> who murdered a veteran patrol agent, portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Wilford_Brimley" title="Wilford Brimley">Wilford Brimley</a>, who had intercepted the smuggler one evening bringing in a shipment of illegal aliens across the border.  Their investigation leads to the breaking up of the vicious smuggling operation run by Harris's character.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Border_Cop" title="Border Cop">Border Cop</a></i>, a 1980 film starring <a href="/wiki/Telly_Savalas" title="Telly Savalas">Telly Savalas</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Border_(1982_film)" title="The Border (1982 film)">The Border</a></i>, a 1982 film starring <a href="/wiki/Jack_Nicholson" title="Jack Nicholson">Jack Nicholson</a> as a patrol agent working on the Mexico-U.S. border.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/El_Norte_(film)" title="El Norte (film)">El Norte</a></i>, a 1983 film about the plight of Central American Indian peasants traveling to the Mexico-U.S. border.</li>
<li>The 1983 movie <i><a href="/wiki/Lone_Wolf_McQuade" title="Lone Wolf McQuade">Lone Wolf McQuade</a></i> deals with smuggling and criminals in various parts of Texas including the Mexico-U.S. border.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Flashpoint_(1984_film)" title="Flashpoint (1984 film)">Flashpoint</a></i>, a 1984 film starring <a href="/wiki/Kris_Kristofferson" title="Kris Kristofferson">Kris Kristofferson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Treat_Williams" title="Treat Williams">Treat Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rip_Torn" title="Rip Torn">Rip Torn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kurtwood_Smith" title="Kurtwood Smith">Kurtwood Smith</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Last_Man_Standing_(1996_film)" title="Last Man Standing (1996 film)">Last Man Standing</a></i>, a 1996 film starring <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Willis" title="Bruce Willis">Bruce Willis</a> as a professional gunman and <a href="/wiki/Ken_Jenkins" title="Ken Jenkins">Ken Jenkins</a> as <a href="/wiki/Texas_Ranger_Division" title="Texas Ranger Division">Texas Ranger</a> Captain Tom Pickett who is investigating the murder of an unnamed patrol inspector (played by Larry Holt) in the town where Willis's character is working.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Men_in_Black_(1997_film)" title="Men in Black (1997 film)">Men in Black</a></i>, a 1997 science fiction comedy action film starring <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lee_Jones" title="Tommy Lee Jones">Tommy Lee Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">Will Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vincent_D%27Onofrio" title="Vincent D&#39;Onofrio">Vincent D'Onofrio</a>. The Border Patrol is portrayed as Immigration Inspectors in an unflattering portrayal.</li>
<li><i>The Gatekeeper</i>, a 2002 film by <a href="/wiki/John_Carlos_Frey" title="John Carlos Frey">John Carlos Frey</a> about the struggles of aliens at the Mexico-U.S. border.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Three_Burials_of_Melquiades_Estrada" title="The Three Burials of Melquiades Estrada">The Three Burials of Melquiades Estrada</a></i>, a 2005 film by <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lee_Jones" title="Tommy Lee Jones">Tommy Lee Jones</a> about the accidental killing of an illegal Mexican alien by a Border Patrol Agent.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Shepherd:_Border_Patrol" title="The Shepherd: Border Patrol">The Shepherd: Border Patrol</a></i>, a 2007 film starring <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Van_Damme" title="Jean-Claude Van Damme">Jean-Claude Van Damme</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Linewatch" title="Linewatch">Linewatch</a></i>, a 2008 film starring <a href="/wiki/Cuba_Gooding,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Cuba Gooding, Jr.">Cuba Gooding, Jr.</a>, as a Border Patrol agent defending his family from a group of Los Angeles gang members involved in narcotics importation.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Hunt_to_Kill" title="Hunt to Kill">Hunt to Kill</a></i>, A 2010 film starring Stone Cold Steve Austin and Eric Roberts as U.S. Border Patrol Agents.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Terminator:_Dark_Fate" title="Terminator: Dark Fate">Terminator: Dark Fate</a></i>, a 2019 science fiction action film starring <a href="/wiki/Linda_Hamilton" title="Linda Hamilton">Linda Hamilton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mackenzie_Davis" title="Mackenzie Davis">Mackenzie Davis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Reyes" title="Natalia Reyes">Natalia Reyes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Luna" title="Gabriel Luna">Gabriel Luna</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Documentaries">Documentaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Border_Patrol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Documentaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><i>Border Patrol: American's Gatekeepers</i>, by <a href="/wiki/A%26E_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="A&amp;E Network">A&amp;E Network</a> with former U.S. Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Janet_Reno" title="Janet Reno">Janet Reno</a>.</li>
<li><i>Investigative Reports: Border Patrol: America's Gatekeepers</i>, by A+E Networks Investigates.</li>
<li><i>History the Enforcers: Border Patrol</i>, by the <a href="/wiki/History_(U.S._TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="History (U.S. TV channel)">History Channel</a>.</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Border_Wars_(TV_series)" title="Border Wars (TV series)">Border Wars</a></i>, a "reality" television program produced by the <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="National Geographic Channel">National Geographic Channel</a>.</li>
<li><i>Run For Your Life</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Canadian Broadcasting Corporation">Canadian Broadcasting Corporation</a> documentary about the dangers faced by young Hondurans aboard a freight train headed to the Mexico-U.S. border, where they will seek illegal entry.</li>
<li><i>Under Siege: America's Northern Border</i> by Discovery Channel.  A 2013 documentary about the efforts and difficulties of agents to prevent illegal cross-border activities in the Detroit, Michigan area.</li></ul>

<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Huspek, Michael; Roberto Martinez; Leticia Jimenez (1998). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://findarticles.com/p/articles/mi_hb3427/is_n2_v25/ai_n28711340/">"Violations of human and civil rights on the U.S.-Mexico border, 1995 to 1997: a report"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(Reprint)</span>. <i>Social Justice</i>. <b>25</b> (2). <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">ISSN</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/1043-1578">1043-1578</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">June 1,</span> 2009</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Justice&amp;rft.atitle=Violations+of+human+and+civil+rights+on+the+U.S.-Mexico+border%2C+1995+to+1997%3A+a+report&amp;rft.volume=25&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.issn=1043-1578&amp;rft.aulast=Huspek&amp;rft.aufirst=Michael&amp;rft.au=Roberto+Martinez&amp;rft.au=Leticia+Jimenez&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Ffindarticles.com%2Fp%2Farticles%2Fmi_hb3427%2Fis_n2_v25%2Fai_n28711340%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUnited+States+Border+Patrol" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"/><p>The data compiled in this report suggest that law enforcement in the southwest region of the United States may be verging on lawlessness. This statement receives fuller support from announcements emanating from the INS. In December 1997, John Chase, head of the INS Office of Internal Audit, announced at a press conference that public complaints to the INS had risen 29% from 1996, with the "vast majority" of complaints emanating from the southwest border region. Over 2,300 complaints were filed in 1997 as opposed to the 1,813 complaints filed in 1996. Another 400 reports of "minor misconduct" were placed in a new category. Chase was quick to emphasize, however, that the 243 "serious" allegations of abuse and use of excessive force that could warrant criminal prosecution were down in 1997, as compared with the 328 in 1996. These "serious" cases are considered to be distinct from less serious complaints, such as "verbal abuse, discrimination, extended detention without cause.</p></span>
</li>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kelly_Lytle_Hernandez" class="mw-redirect" title="Kelly Lytle Hernandez">Kelly Lytle Hernandez</a>. <i>Migra! A History of the U.S. Border Patrol</i>  (University of California Press; 2010) 274 pages; draws on previously lost and untapped records in a history of the force since its beginnings in 1924.</li></ul>
